# for Emacs: -*- coding: utf-8 -*-
#
# User-defined key sequences for WinCompose
# by Sam Hocevar <sam@hocevar.net>
#

# Key sequences have the following form:
#
#<Multi_key> <key>… : "resulting text"
#
# All key names must be enclosed in <angle brackets>.
# The first key must be <Multi_key>.
# The remaining keys can be single characters, like <a>, <B>, <7>,
# <.>, <@>, or from the following list:
#
#     Up, Down, Left, Right (the arrow keys), space, exclam, quotedbl,
#     numbersign, dollar, percent, ampersand, apostrophe, parenleft,
#     parenright, asterisk, plus, comma, minus, period, slash, colon,
#     semicolon, less, equal, greater, at, bracketleft, backslash,
#     bracketright, asciicircum, underscore, grave, braceleft, bar,
#     braceright, asciitilde.
#
# For more definitions, see the files in C:\Program Files\WinCompose\res.



# UTF-8 (Unicode) compose sequence
# David.Monniaux@ens.fr
#

# Part 1 - Manual definitions

# Spacing versions of dead accents
#<Multi_key> <'> <'> 	: "´"   acute # ACUTE ACCENT (DB: removed to avoid conflict with LEFT DOUBLE QUOTATION MARK)
#<Multi_key> <-> <^> 	: "¯"   macron # MACRON (DB: removed to avoid conflict with UPWARDS ARROW)
<Multi_key> <Multi_key> <^> <_> <space> 	: "¯"   macron # MACRON (DB: changed to avoid conflict with SUPERSCRIPT MINUS, and multi key to avoid conflict with COMBINING OVERLINE)
<Multi_key> <Multi_key> <_> <_> <space>	: "¯"   macron # MACRON (DB: space added to avoid conflict with MATHEMATICAL LEFT FLATTENED PARENTHESIS and MATHEMATICAL RIGHT FLATTENED PARENTHESIS, and multi key to avoid conflict with COMBINING UNDERLINE)
<Multi_key> <Multi_key> <_> <^> <space> 	: "¯"   macron # MACRON (DB: space added to avoid conflict with UP ARROWHEAD BETWEEN TWO HORIZONTAL BARS; aka ENTER KEY, aka NOT AMUSED, and multi key to avoid conflict with COMBINING OVERLINE and LOW LINE (undirected value))
<Multi_key> <space> <(>		: "˘"   breve # BREVE
<Multi_key> <(> <space>		: "˘"   breve # BREVE
<Multi_key> <Multi_key> <"> <"> 	: "¨"   diaeresis # DIAERESIS (DB: multi key added to avoid conflict with MUSICAL SYMBOL SHORT BARLINE)
<Multi_key> <space> <less> 		: "ˇ"   caron # CARON
<Multi_key> <less> <space> 		: "ˇ"   caron # CARON
#<Multi_key> <Multi_key> <-> <-> <space>	: "­"   U00ad # SOFT HYPHEN (DB: rmoved to avoid conflict with # EN DASH (followed by space) and wilson minus)

# ASCII characters that may be difficult to access
# on some keyboards.
<Multi_key> <+> <+>        	: "#"   numbersign # NUMBER SIGN
#<Multi_key> <'> <space> 	: "'"   apostrophe # APOSTROPHE (DB: removed to avoid conflict with RIGHT SINGLE QUOTATION MARK)
#<Multi_key> <space> <'> 	: "'"   apostrophe # APOSTROPHE (DB: removed to avoid conflict with space followed by LEFT SINGLE QUOTATION MARK)
<Multi_key> <A> <T>              	: "@"   at # COMMERCIAL AT
<Multi_key> <(> <(> 	: "["   bracketleft # LEFT SQUARE BRACKET
#<Multi_key> </> </>      	: "\\"   backslash # REVERSE SOLIDUS (DB: changed to avoid conflict with FRACTION SLASH)
<Multi_key> </> <less>       	: "\\"   backslash # REVERSE SOLIDUS
<Multi_key> <less> </>       	: "\\"   backslash # REVERSE SOLIDUS
<Multi_key> <)> <)> 	: "]"   bracketright # RIGHT SQUARE BRACKET

<Multi_key> <^> <space> 	: "^"   asciicircum # CIRCUMFLEX ACCENT
<Multi_key> <space> <^> 	: "^"   asciicircum # CIRCUMFLEX ACCENT
<Multi_key> <greater> <space>    	: "^"   asciicircum # CIRCUMFLEX ACCENT
<Multi_key> <space> <greater>    	: "^"   asciicircum # CIRCUMFLEX ACCENT

#<Multi_key> <`> <space>      	: "`"   grave # GRAVE ACCENT (DB: removed to avoid conflict with LEFT SINGLE QUOTATION MARK)
#<Multi_key> <space> <'>      	: "`"   grave # GRAVE ACCENT (DB: removed to avoid conflict with space followed by LEFT SINGLE QUOTATION MARK)

#<Multi_key> <,> <space>      	: "¸"   cedilla # CEDILLA (DB: removed to avoid conflict with SINGLE LOW-9 QUOTATION MARK)
<Multi_key> <space> <,>      	: "¸"   cedilla # CEDILLA
#<Multi_key> <,> <,> 		: "¸"   cedilla # CEDILLA (DB: removed to avoid conflict with DOUBLE LOW-9 QUOTATION MARK)

<Multi_key> <(> <-> <space>  	: "{"   braceleft # LEFT CURLY BRACKET (DB: space added to avoid conflict with CIRCLED MINUS)
#<Multi_key> <-> <(>  	: "{"   braceleft # LEFT CURLY BRACKET (DB: removed to avoid conflict with SUBSCRIPT LEFT PARENTHESIS)

<Multi_key> </> <^> 	: "|"   bar # VERTICAL LINE
<Multi_key> <^> </> 	: "|"   bar # VERTICAL LINE
<Multi_key> <V> <L>              	: "|"   bar # VERTICAL LINE
<Multi_key> <L> <V>              	: "|"   bar # VERTICAL LINE
<Multi_key> <v> <l>              	: "|"   bar # VERTICAL LINE
<Multi_key> <l> <v>              	: "|"   bar # VERTICAL LINE

<Multi_key> <)> <-> 	: "}"   braceright # RIGHT CURLY BRACKET
#<Multi_key> <-> <)> 	: "}"   braceright # RIGHT CURLY BRACKET (DB: removed to avoid conflict with SUBSCRIPT RIGHT PARENTHESIS)

<Multi_key> <~> <space> 	: "~"   asciitilde # TILDE
<Multi_key> <space> <~> 	: "~"   asciitilde # TILDE
#<Multi_key> <-> <space>      	: "~"   asciitilde # TILDE (DB: removed to avoid conflict with EM DASH)
#<Multi_key> <space> <->      	: "~"   asciitilde # TILDE (DB: removed to avoid conflict with EM DASH surrounded by THIN SPACEs.)

# Part 2

# Compose map for Korean Hangul(Choseongul) Conjoining Jamos  automatically
# generated  from UnicodeData-2.0.14.txt at
#    ftp://ftp.unicode.org/Public/2.0-Update/UnicodeData-2.0.14.txt
#   by Jungshik Shin <jshin@jshin.net>  2002-10-17
# There are some conflicts among sequences, but I left them alone.
#
# group 1: cluster jamos made of three basic jamos

# APL support Geoff Streeter 2012-01-04

# APL was initially an overstruck language. The original APL terminal was an IBM golfball
# with a specially designed golfball. This meant that characters could be overstruck to
# produce other characters. This gave APL a richness of primitives which is still powerful
# today. Overstrikes were always independent of order.

# APLs have extended this into a number of dialects. Let us try to support lots of them.
# Together with some that have not been used yet. Some traditional ones are not included.

# Characters from "Mathematical Operators"

<Multi_key> <v> </>                         : "√"   U221a   # v / SQUARE ROOT
<Multi_key> </> <v>                         : "√"   U221a   # / v SQUARE ROOT
<Multi_key> <8> <8>                             : "∞"   U221e   # 8 8 INFINITY
<Multi_key> <=> <_>                : "≡"   U2261   # = _ IDENTICAL TO

<Multi_key> <U2260> <_>                : "≢"   U2262   # ≠ _ NOT IDENTICAL TO
<Multi_key> <less> <_>                 : "≤"   U2264   # < _ LESS-THAN OR EQUAL TO
<Multi_key> <_> <less> <space>                 : "≤"   U2264   # _ < LESS-THAN OR EQUAL TO (DB: space added to avoid conflict with LEFT TACK)

# These two are already present for me:
#<Multi_key> <-> <-> <->	: "—"	U2014		# EM DASH

#<Multi_key> <-> <-> <space>	: "– "			# EN DASH (followed by space) (DB: removed because would be intercepted by subscript minus)
<Multi_key> <Multi_key> <D> <-> <~> <-> : "―" U2015 # HORIZONTAL BAR (DB: multi key added to avoid conflict with MODIFIER LETTER LOW TILDE (subscript tilde), and D added to avoid conflict with wilson minus)
<Multi_key> <Multi_key> <D> <-> <2> <M> 	 : "⸺" U2E3A # TWO-EM DASH (DB: multi key added to avoid conflict with SUBSCRIPT 2, and D added to avoid conflict with wilson minus)
<Multi_key> <Multi_key> <D> <-> <3> <M>	 	 : "⸻" U2E3B # THREE-EM DASH (DB: multi key added to avoid conflict with SUBSCRIPT 3, and D added to avoid conflict with wilson minus)
<Multi_key> <Multi_key> <\> <->		: "­"	U00AD		# SOFT HYPHEN (DB: changed to avoid conflict with COMBINING LONG STROKE OVERLAY)
# This is the recommended typographical practice for em dashes in English.
# Unfortunately, it doesn’t work out all that well in monospace fonts,
# where the thin spaces aren’t thin.  But I think this is okay.
# This conflicts with the default binding to “~”, which is potentially
# a problem for non-American keyboards.
<Multi_key> <space> <->             : " — "                 # EM DASH surrounded by THIN SPACEs.

# Convenience shortcuts for quotation marks.
<Multi_key> <space> <">          : " “"                  # space followed by LEFT DOUBLE QUOTATION MARK
<Multi_key> <"> <space>          : "” "                  # RIGHT DOUBLE QUOTATION MARK followed by space
<Multi_key> <space> <'>        : " ‘"                # space followed by LEFT SINGLE QUOTATION MARK
# Unfortunately <'> <space> is, asymmetrically, just "’".  Whatever.
<Multi_key> <n> <t>                     : "n’t "              # Apostrophized English “not.”

    # himself in “A view of the history of the ISO character code”, 1972

# The system file gives us subscript numbers, plus/minus, and parens.  But
# there are letters missing.  It would be nice to have at least a few of them.

# block U+208x
<Multi_key> <_> <0>  	       : "₀"  U2080   	  # SUBSCRIPT ZERO

<Multi_key> <_> <)>           : "₎"  U208E	  # SUBSCRIPT RIGHT PARENTHESIS

# Some archaic Greek.  If we only wanted *normal* characters we wouldn't be
# doing this at all!
# "period" will indicate a sort of variant of some kind; asterisk is still the "greek" marker

# Custom additions: for chat (kragen)
<Multi_key> <(> <:>         : "☻"   U263B           # BLACK SMILING FACE
<Multi_key> <:> <)>        : "☺"   U263A           # WHITE SMILING FACE
<Multi_key> <:> <(>         : "☹"   U2639           # WHITE FROWNING FACE
<Multi_key> <:> <~>	: "⍨"   U2368		# APL FUNCTIONAL SYMBOL TILDE DIAERESIS
<Multi_key> <:> <|>		: "⸚"   U2E1A		# HYPHEN WITH DIAERESIS
<Multi_key> <:> <o> <o> <)>  :  "°͜°"    # Funny smiley-face.
# Those are archaic cyrilic letters... but look so _perfect_ for use
# in chat. And about the last, the "multiocular O"... Well, I don't
# know what it can be used for, but given the description, how could I
# leave it out‽
# (I guess using U+1F440 EYES would be more straightforward, but not as funny?)
<Multi_key> <O> <.> <O>		: "Ꙭ"	UA66C		# CYRILLIC CAPITAL LETTER DOUBLE MONOCULAR O * used in the dual of words based on the root for 'eye'

# aren't important enough for the real dotXcompose, but if you want them,
# you can always include them using the include directive.
#
# My .XCompose is not a link to this repository's dotXcompose; it starts with
# include "/path/to/.XCompose_std"
# ... (which *is* a symlink to dotXcompose), and then also includes the 
# frakturcompose file, and defines some idiosyncratic ones of my own.

# Dave Keenan's custom additions
# Useful Unicode searches: http://www.fileformat.info/info/unicode/char/search.htm
# https://unicode-search.net/unicode-namesearch.pl
# X.org compose sequences: https://www.x.org/releases/X11R7.7/doc/libX11/i18n/compose/en_US.UTF-8.html

# The old assignment of no-break spaces that Mike is used to.
#<Multi_key> <space> <space>	: " "	U00A0	# NO-BREAK SPACE (Don't uncomment. Already defined)
#<Multi_key> <Multi_key> <space>: " "	U202F	# NARROW NO-BREAK SPACE

# The new assignment of no-break spaces that Dave prefers because it obeys the mnemonic rule
# where all the most common sequences consist of Compose followed by a double-character.
<Multi_key> <space> <space>	: " "	U202F	# NARROW NO-BREAK SPACE (overrides no-break space)
<Multi_key> <Multi_key> <space>	: " "	U00A0	# NO-BREAK SPACE

<Multi_key> <space> <1>		: " "	U2007	# FIGURE SPACE (same width as a digit)
<Multi_key> <space> <T>		: " "	U2009	# THIN SPACE
<Multi_key> <space> <H>		: " "	U200A	# HAIR SPACE
<Multi_key> <space> <+>		: "⁤"	U2064	# INVISIBLE PLUS (use before FRACTION SLASH to make mixed fractions)
<Multi_key> <0> <0>		: "°"	U0080	# DEGREE SIGN
<Multi_key> <1> <1>    		: "⁻¹"	U207B U00B9 # SUPERSCRIPT MINUS, SUPERSCRIPT ONE
<Multi_key> <2> <2>    		: "²"	U00B2	# SUPERSCRIPT TWO
<Multi_key> <3> <3>    		: "³"	U00B3	# SUPERSCRIPT THREE
<Multi_key> <4> <4>    		: "⁴"	U2074	# SUPERSCRIPT FOUR
<Multi_key> <5> <5>    		: "⁵"	U2075	# SUPERSCRIPT FIVE
<Multi_key> <7> <7>    		: "⁷"	U2077	# SUPERSCRIPT SEVEN
#<Multi_key> <8> <8>		: "∞"	U221E	# INFINITY  (built-in)
<Multi_key> <n> <n>		: "ⁿ"	U207F	# SUPERSCRIPT LATIN SMALL LETTER N
#<Multi_key> <v> </>		: "√"	U221A	# SQUARE ROOT (built-in)
<Multi_key> <@> <@>		: "√"	U221A	# SQUARE ROOT (@ is shifted 2)
<Multi_key> <3> <v> </>		: "∛"	U221B	# CUBE ROOT
<Multi_key> <4> <v> </>		: "∜"	U221C	# FOURTH ROOT
<Multi_key> <t> <t>		: "†"	U2020	# DAGGER
<Multi_key> <T> <t>		: "‡"	U2021	# DOUBLE DAGGER
<Multi_key> <t> <T>		: "‡"	U2021	# DOUBLE DAGGER
<Multi_key> <.> <space>		: "• " U2022 U0020 # BULLET, SPACE (alt alt . is Sagittal grave)
<Multi_key> <Multi_key> <Multi_key>: "⎄" U2384	# COMPOSITION SYMBOL (to represent compose key)
#<Multi_key> <\> <space>	: "␣"	U2423	# OPEN BOX (to represent spacebar) (built-in)
#<Multi_key> <\> <\>		: "⏎"	U23CE	# RETURN SYMBOL (to represent Return or Enter key) (DB: removed to avoid intercepting 8 or so other rules)
<Multi_key> <\> <A>		: "⌥"	U2325	# OPTION SYMBOL (to represent Option or Alt key)
<Multi_key> <\> <B>		: "⌫"	U232B	# ERASE TO THE LEFT (to represent Backspace key)
<Multi_key> <\> <C>		: "✲"	U2732	# OPEN CENTRE ASTERISK (to represent Control key)
<Multi_key> <\> <D>		: "⌦"	U2326	# ERASE TO THE RIGHT (to represent Delete key)
<Multi_key> <\> <E>		: "⎋"	U238B	# BROKEN CIRCLE WITH NORTHWEST ARROW (to represent Escape key)
<Multi_key> <\> <.> <E>		: "⏎"	U23CE	# RETURN SYMBOL (to represent Return or Enter key)
<Multi_key> <\> <L>		: "⇪"	U21EA	# UPWARDS WHITE ARROW FROM BAR (to represent Caps Lock key)
<Multi_key> <\> <O>		: "⌥"	U2325	# OPTION SYMBOL (to represent Option or Alt key)
<Multi_key> <\> <R>		: "⏎"	U23CE	# RETURN SYMBOL (to represent Return or Enter key)
<Multi_key> <\> <S>		: "⇧"	U21E7	# SHIFT SYMBOL (to represent Shift key)
<Multi_key> <\> <T>		: "⭾"	U2B7E	# HORIZONTAL TAB KEY (to represent Tab key)
<Multi_key> <\> <Up>		: "▲"	U25B2	# BLACK UP-POINTING TRIANGLE (to represent up-arrow key)
<Multi_key> <\> <Right>		: "▶︎" U25B6 UFE0E # BLACK RIGHT-POINTING TRIANGLE (to represent right-arrow key), text variation selector to prevent emoji
<Multi_key> <\> <Down>		: "▼"	U25BC	# BLACK DOWN-POINTING TRIANGLE (to represent down-arrow key)
<Multi_key> <\> <Left>		: "◀︎" U25C0 UFE0E # BLACK LEFT-POINTING TRIANGLE (to represent left-arrow key), text variation selector to prevent emoji
<Multi_key> <|> <Left>		: "⇤"	U21E4	# LEFTWARDS ARROW TO BAR
<Multi_key> <Up> <Down>		: "↕︎" U25B2 UFE0E # UP DOWN ARROW, text variation selector to prevent emoji
<Multi_key> <Down> <Up>		: "↕︎" U25B2 UFE0E # UP DOWN ARROW, text variation selector to prevent emoji
<Multi_key> <Down> <Multi_key> <Up>: "⇵" U21F5	# DOWN ARROW LEFT OF UP ARROW
<Multi_key> <Up> <Multi_key> <Down>: "⇅" U21C5	# UP ARROW LEFT OF DOWN ARROW
<Multi_key> <^> <_>		: "̅"	U0305	# COMBINING OVERLINE (vinculum for fractions, roots etc)
<Multi_key> <_> <_>		: "̲" U0332	# COMBINING LOW LINE (underlining)
<Multi_key> <_> <^>		: "̲̅" U0305 U0332 # COMBINING OVERLINE and LOW LINE (undirected value)
#<Multi_key> <_> <->		: "̲̅" U0305 U0332 # COMBINING OVERLINE and LOW LINE (undirected value) (DB: removing to avoid conflict with SUBSCRIPT MINUS)
<Multi_key> <-> <_>		: "̲̅" U0305 U0332 # COMBINING OVERLINE and LOW LINE (undirected value)
<Multi_key> <;> <;>		: "̲̅" U0305 U0332 # COMBINING OVERLINE and LOW LINE (undirected value)
<Multi_key> <\> <->		: "̶"	U0336	# COMBINING LONG STROKE OVERLAY (strike-thru) (overrides soft hyphen built-in)
<Multi_key> <.> <->		: "­"	U00AD	# SOFT HYPHEN
<Multi_key> <:> <:>	: "÷"	U00F7	# DIVISION SIGN
#<Multi_key> <|> <_> <->	: "⏚"	U23DA	# EARTH GROUND (this is overridden by the LEFT FLOOR sequence)
<Multi_key> <|> <-> <_>		: "⏚"	U23DA	# EARTH GROUND
<Multi_key> <L> <L>		: "⅂"	U2142	# TURNED UPPERCASE L
<Multi_key> <L> <BackSpace>		: "⅃"	U2143	# REVERSED UPPERCASE L (DB: changed to avoid conflict LATIN CAPITAL LETTER L WITH CARON)
<Multi_key> <b> <b>		: "♭"	U266D	# MUSIC FLAT SIGN
<Multi_key> <d> <d> 		: "∂"	U2202	# PARTIAL DIFFERENTIAL
#<Multi_key> <e> <e>		: "ə"	U0259	# LATIN SMALL LETTER SCHWA (built-in)
<Multi_key> <i> <i>		: "ɪ"	U026A	# LATIN LETTER SMALL CAPITAL I
#<Multi_key> <f> <f>		: "ϕ"	U03D5	# GREEK PHI SYMBOL (straight phi) (DB: removed to avoid conflict with LATIN SMALL LIGATURE FF)

# SI Unit and multiplier symbols preceded by a narrow no-break space. Prefix <space>.
# I don't have one for H for henry because that's the sequence for hair space.
# I don't have one for M for mega because that's the sequence for em space.
# I don't have one for N for newton because that's the sequence for en space.
# I don't have one for T for tera because that's the sequence for thin space.
# Figure space is <Multi_key> <space> <1>

# Greek letters. Prefix <8> is <*> without shift. The asterisk suggests the circular "Greek key" pattern in Greek art.
# As with all non-Latin alphabets in this document, this keyboard layout is based on homophony (similarity of sound)
# where possible. In the two cases where no Latin letter with that sound exists, 
# it is based on letter-shape: Q for theta and Y for psi. 
# We use the Adobe Symbol-font mapping (also used by Wolfram Language). 
# See Adobe's mapping here: http://www.sscnet.ucla.edu/soc/faculty/mcfarland/soc281/symbol.htm
# And Wolfram's here: https://reference.wolfram.com/language/tutorial/InputAndOutputInNotebooks.html#14875
#
#        ----- ----- ----- ----- ----- ----- ----- ----- ----- ----- -----
#       |     |     |cyril|hebrw|frakt|super|scrip|GREEK|bold |italc|subsc|
#       | 1   | 2   | 3   | 4   | 5   | 6   | 7   | 8 ∞ | 9   | 0   | -   |
#        -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- ----- -----
#          | Q Θ | W Ω | E Ε | R Ρ | T Τ | Y Ψ | U Υ | I Ι | O Ο | P Π | {   | }   | |   |
#          | q θ | w ω | e ε | r ρ | t τ | y ψ | u υ | i ι | o ο | p π |sans |mono |doubl|
#           - --- - --- - --- - --- - --- - --- - --- - --- - --- - --- ----- ----- -----
#            | A Α | S Σ | D Δ | F Φ | G Γ | H Η | J ϑ | K Κ | L Λ |
#            | a α | s σ | d δ | f ϕ | g γ | h η | j φ | k κ | l λ |
#             - --- - --- - --- - --- - --- - --- - --- - --- -----
#              | Z Ζ | X Ξ | C Χ | V ς | B Β | N Ν | M Μ | 
#              | z ζ | x ξ | c χ | v ϖ | b β | n ν | m μ |
#               ----- ----- ----- ----- ----- ----- -----
#
# Since the Greek alphabet only has 24 letters, Jj and Vv are used for some variant forms. These and other
# variant forms and related math symbols can also be obtained by typing a period (and sometimes two periods)
# before the letter. The form obtained without typing a period is the form used most often in mathematics,
# which is not necessarily the form used most often in Greek language text. It is the form not considered a
# variant by TeX and not considered "curly" by Wolfram Language, except in the case of small epsilon. TeX is
# simply wrong about epsilon, and the above-referenced version of the Symbol font is right. The lunate form is
# rarely used as a variable because it looks too much like the "ELEMENT OF" or \in symbol.
# * There is a completely different problem with small letter phi. The form obtained without typing a period
# is intended to be the straight phi (TeX agrees that's the standard math form), but some fonts will give the
# curly form, because the Unicode comitteee screwed up and showed the curly form as the reference glyph until
# Unicode version 3. The form obtained by typing a period remains at the whim of the font designer.
# So if you don't get the expected form of phi, don't switch to the other character, find a font that gives
# the correct result.

# Reserved for Mathematical Sans-serif italic letters. Prefix <{> <0>.
# Reserved for Mathematical Sans-serif bold italic letters. Prefix <{> <9> <0>.
# Reserved for Mathematical Sans-serif bold Greek letters. Prefix <{> <9> <8>.

# Hebrew alphabet and mathematical symbols. Prefix <4>.
# This Hebrew keyboard layout is based on homophony (similarity of sound) where possible. 
# It incorporates ideas from the following:
# https://web.archive.org/web/20210419023909/https://egarc.ku.edu/installing-hebrew-ku-homophonic-keyboard-windows-7
# https://jakebinstein.com/blog/customizable-hebrew-phonetic-keyboard-for-windows-10-8-7/
# https://www.lexilogos.com/keyboard/hebrew.htm
#
#  ----- ----- ----- ----- ----- ----- ----- ----- ----- ----- ----- ----- -----
# | ~   |     |     |cyril|HEBRW|frakt|super|scrip|greek|bold |italc|subsc| +   |
# | `   | 1   | 2   | 3   | 4   | 5   | 6   | 7   | 8   | 9   | 0   | - ־‎ | =   |
#  ----- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -----
#          | Q   | W שׂ | E   | R   | T ט | Y   | U   | I   | O   | P   | {   | }   | | ׀ |
#          | q ק | w שׁ | e ע | r ר | t ת | y ט | u ו | i י | o ו | p פּ |sans |mono |doubl|
#           - --- - --- - --- - --- - --- - --- - --- - --- - --- - --- - --- - --- -----
#            | A ℵ | S ש | D  ℸ  | F ף | G  ℷ  | H ח | J   | K ך | L   | : ׃‎ | " ״ |
#            | a א | s ס | d ד | f פ | g ג | h ה | j ח | k כ | l ל‎ | ;   | ' ׳ |
#             - --- - --- - --- - --- - --- - --- - --- - --- ----- ----- -----
#              | Z   | X ץ | C ץ | V   | B ℶ  | N ן | M ם |
#              | z ז | x צ | c צ | v ו | b ב | n נ | m מ |
#               ----- ----- ----- ----- ----- ----- -----
#
# Hebrew is written from right to left.
# The Hebrew alphabet has 22 letters and no case. But 5 letters have different final forms, 
# so shift is used to access these, as well as the mathematical-symbol versions of Alef, Bet, Gimel, Dalet.
# Shift also gives access to Het, Tet and dotless Shin on homophonic keys which otherwise give he, tav and samekh.
# Het, tet, and shin are also available unshifted, as j, y and w, chosen because j and y are 
# immediately to the right of the homophonic keys and w has a similar letter shape.
# Shift-W is used for sin (shin with left dot).
# Shifted vowels EIOUY are reserved for possible future implementation of nikud. 
# Also available for nikud are shifted JLPQRVZ~{} and unshifted `[]\;

# Zero width characters that allow overriding the Unicode bidirectional algorithm when necessary.
<Multi_key> <4> <Right>	: "‎"	U200E	# LEFT-TO-RIGHT MARK
<Multi_key> <4> <Left>	: "‏"	U200F	# RIGHT-TO-LEFT MARK

# The four Hebrew mathematical symbols (use the shift key):
<Multi_key> <4> <A>		: "ℵ"	U2135	# ALEF SYMBOL (first transfinite cardinal)
<Multi_key> <4> <B>		: "ℶ"	U2136	# BET SYMBOL (second transfinite cardinal)
<Multi_key> <4> <G>		: "ℷ"	U2137	# GIMEL SYMBOL (third transfinite cardinal)
<Multi_key> <4> <D>		: "ℸ"	U2138	# DALET SYMBOL (fourth transfinite cardinal)

# Cyrillic alphabet (Russian, Ukrainian, Belarusian, Bulgarian). Prefix <3>.
# The Russian alphabet of 33 characters is mapped to the Latin keyboard as shown below, 
# which is based on similarity of sound where possible. It uses the popular "Student" mapping
# supported by the American Association of Teachers of Slavic and East European Languages.
# https://www.aatseel.org/resources/fonts/windows_cyrillic.htm#keyboard
#
#  ----- ----- ----- ----- ----- ----- ----- ----- ----- ----- ----- ----- -----
# | ~ Ё |     |     |CYRIL|hebrw|frakt|super|scrip|greek|bold |italc|subsc| + Ъ |
# | ` ё | 1   | 2   | 3   | 4   | 5   | 6   | 7   | 8   | 9   | 0   | -   | = ъ |
#  ----- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -----
#          | Q Я | W Ш | E Е | R Р | T Т | Y Ы | U У | I И | O О | P П | { Ю | } Щ | | Э |
#          | q я | w ш | e е | r р | t т | y ы | u у | i и | o о | p п | [ ю | ] щ | \ э |
#           - --- - --- - --- - --- - --- - --- - --- - --- - --- - --- - --- - --- -----
#            | A А | S С | D Д | F Ф | G Г | H Ч | J Й | K К | L Л | : Ь | " Ж |
#            | a а | s с | d д | f ф | g г | h ч | j й | k к | l л | ; ь | ' Ж |
#             - --- - --- - --- - --- - --- - --- - --- - --- ----- ----- -----
#              | Z З | X Х | C Ц | V В | B Б | N Н | M М |
#              | z з | x х | c ц | v в | b б | n н | m м |
#               ----- ----- ----- ----- ----- ----- -----
#
# The Ukranian alphabet of 33 characters is obtained by omitting `~ =+ \|
# and replacing y Y with .y .Y, and adding .e .E .g .G .i .I.
# The Belarusian alphabet of 32 characters is obtained by omitting =+ ]}
# and replacing i I with .i .I, and adding .u .U.
# The Bulgarian alphabet of 30 characters is obtained by omitting `~ \| yY.

# Reserved for Arabic Mathematical (isolated) letters and Arabic-Indic digits. Prefix <+>
# Reserved for Arabic Mathematical (isolated) dotless letters. Prefix <+> <.>
# Reserved for Arabic Mathematical initial letters. Prefix <+> <0>
# Reserved for Arabic Mathematical tailed letters. Prefix <+> <9>
# Reserved for Arabic Mathematical tailed dotless letters. Prefix <+> <9> <.>
# Reserved for Arabic Mathematical stretched letters. Prefix <+> <5>
# Reserved for Arabic Mathematical stretched dotless letters. Prefix <+> <5> <.>
# Reserved for Arabic Mathematical looped letters. Prefix <+> <7>
# Reserved for Arabic Mathematical double-struck letters. Prefix <+> <|>
# There are 28 letters in the Arabic mathematical abjad. Hamza, the 29th is omitted.
# As with Hebrew, Arabic is written left to right, and there are no capital letters, 
# so shift can be used to access different letters with the same or similar Latin homophone. 
# Near-homophonic keyboard map in abjad order: abjdhwzHTyklmnsAfSqrctpxvDZgQ
# Keys not used: e i o u. Letters not used BCEFGIJKLMNOPQRUVWXY
# The o, u and - keys should not be used, due to built-in sequences where they are prefixed by +.
# Could use ;: and '" and [{ and ]} keys.
#
#  ----- ----- ----- ----- ----- ----- ----- ----- ----- ----- ----- ----- -----
# | ~   |     |     |cyril|hebrw|frakt|super|scrip|greek|bold |italc|subsc| +   |
# | `   | 1   | 2   | 3   | 4   | 5   | 6   | 7   | 8   | 9   | 0   | -  ‎ |ARABC|
#  ----- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -- -----
#          | Q   | W   | E   | R   | T   | Y   | U   | I   | O   | P   | {   | }   | |   |
#          | q   | w   | e   | r   | t   | y   | u   | i   | o   | p   |sans |mono |doubl|
#           - --- - --- - --- - --- - --- - --- - --- - --- - --- - --- - --- - --- -----
#            | A   | S   | D   | F   | G  | H   | J   | K   | L   | :  ‎ | "   |
#            | a   | s   | d   | f   | g  | h   | j   | k   | l   | ;   | '   |
#             - --- - --- - --- - --- - --- - --- - --- - --- ----- ----- -----
#              | Z   | X   | C   | V   | B   | N   | M   |
#              | z   | x   | c   | v   | b   | n   | m   |
#               ----- ----- ----- ----- ----- ----- -----
#
# Zero width characters that allow overriding the Unicode bidirectional algorithm when necessary.
<Multi_key> <+> <Right>	: "‎"	U200E	# LEFT-TO-RIGHT MARK
